If you like sour beer this is a MUST VISIT. If you don't like sour beer, well you're in luck because their other beers are also excellent. There's almost always a food truck here serving up something delicious, and the patio has tons of space to hang out. There's often events going on here and they're always a great time. <Time>1617739134343<//Time><rate>5< /rate><Text>Great microbrewery in Downtown Santa Rosa. It's kind of easy to miss since they are tucked on a side street at the south end of the mall, but a must-visit for specialty beer lovers. They always have a variety of really interesting options, including sour beers and other unique variations outside the typical IPAs. The tasting room is spacious, staff are really friendly and helpful. I love stopping in and watching them can my beer right in front of me before I take it home to enjoy. I'm looking forward to when they have live music again.< /Text>< pictures>

<review>What an enjoyable visit! Only tried one of their brews, but it was delicious. Interesting setup, cool little lounge area next to the bar complete with comfy couches and a row of old school movie theater seats. Nice patio out back that backs right up to the creek. Food truck on the patio was offering good-looking Asian dishes while we were there. Most of the space inside holds there brews being aged in barrels, giving the place an industrial warehouse feel. Loved the staff and vibe, will definitely be back for more!</review>< pics>

< review>
What a fun little warehouse bar food truck music venue combo. Very spacious open space, also has tables where you can enjoy a brew and play board games. Live music too! A bit of a walk from the rest of town that's more happening, but it's not really that far a walk from the main square so not an obstacle at all. Worth making your way over.</review>

<username>Ismael Pohlert<//username><time>1603090733167<//time><Rate>5<//Rate>< review>
I went here last night with my parents to celebrate my dads birthday. My parents had been to The Plot, but this was my first time! We ordered family style and shared two appetizers alongside three entrees.

Appetizers: We ordered the roasted cauliflower and takoyaki. The roasted cauliflower was delicious and was served with this gravy-like sauce that was delicious! The takoyaki is a vegan hush puppy and is great with the sauces it sits in. I personally would like a crunchier texture, but it still was enjoyable!

Entrees: My mom ordered the chicken and waffles. My dad ordered the chorizo and polenta. I ordered the stuffed yam. We shared these three dishes and they were all full of great flavors. The chicken and waffles seemed to be a tofu-based chicken that you can dip in a habanero sauce. The waffle was so good and packed with cinnamon goodness. The chorizo and polenta was delicious and the flavors of the chorizo were absorbed perfectly by the polenta. The stuffed yam was insanely good! The topping tastes just like sausage and gravy that you would get on top of biscuits. The sweetness from the yam mixes in a symphony of flavor with the savory topping!

Service & Ambience: We made reservations and were brought to a table as soon as we arrived at the hostess table. Our server was Lori and she was very helpful. Lori provided a free appetizer, extra sauces, and fun stories. Her favorite dish is the stuffed yam and she was stoked I chose that dish! The ambience at the restaurant is peaceful and the outdoor seating is nicely set up. I will definitely be coming back here for the stuffed yam and to try some new dishes!< /review>

<response>None< /response>< Text>
Honestly, my biggest complaint about this place is that they aren't closer to east county. ü§∑üèº‚Äç‚ôÇÔ∏è But I'd definitely spend half a tank of gas to come here again. üôÉ I came with my Dad and this was his first full vegan meal and he's a steak n potatoes, midwestern boi so I was eager to see his reaction to it.

*THERE IS A SMALL PARKING LOT BEHIND THE RESTAURANT THROUGH A CHAIN LINK FENCE WITH A BLUE SIGN TO THE LEFT OF IT THAT SAYS THE PLOT* Don't miss it like my Dad did, mkay? üôÉ

Got there and a decent dinner service going on. Quickly sat by the hostess and greeted by our lovely server (Jen was it? ü§î). Ordered a couple drinks and the tak√∂yaki "kind of hush puppies". My Dad ordered kombucha (which he's never had before) and actually enjoyed it (I mean, what's not to like üòè). The hush puppies were off the chain!  Warm and slightly crispy outside with a soft and flakey inside paired with a cold slaw that offers an awesome contrast of sweet/salty, warm/chilled, soft/crunchy, and some zip in the flavor as well. A very well balanced starter! Dad's opinion - he liked it! Off to a good start!
Next up, we both ordered the fresh heart of palm stir fry. This dish was amazing! And my Dad loved it too! The presentation had a lot of pop to it - although I would've liked smaller pieces of the yellow pickles; they were a little tough to cut and large slices (gorgeous garnish tho). The dull butter knives had a hard time getting through the "pickle". BUT definitely not a reason for me to ding them, this dish was still on point! The contrast is texture was awesome! Plenty of crunch and chew. Flavors were spot on as well. I usually add some sort of sauce to most restaurant meals but this one didn't need it! I was full by the time I was nearing my last few bites but I couldn't stop. So I sit here type this overstuffed. #NoRagrets

At the finish of the meal we were offered desert but I was trying to make peace with the fact that i couldn't even finish my beer, I was so full. But our awesome server brought us two complimentary wellness shots that were a very potent blend of veggie/fruit juices and couple dry pepper types.

Let me tell you people now, I've taken some wellness shots in my day and I thought I could handle whatever they threw at me. But I was not prepared for that one. That shot was one spicy boi going down and for minutes after. But yo, that was still delicious tho. üôÉ

All in all, this place was great! I'll have to find some time and someone to take to this spot when I can! Definitely worth the drive!<//Text>

< Text>
Great exhibition space in Little Tokyo.  The galleries are larger in scale than the downtown location of MOCA, allowing for more diversity in the exhibitions.  No permanent collection at the Geffen, so check the website to see what's on view.  Exhibitions vary in quality and scope.  Note that a ticket bought at the Geffen will also get you into the downtown branch the same day, and vice versa.</Text>

The idea of The Geffen sounded a lot better than it actually turned out to be with the described converted historic warehouse space. From the moment we entered the difficult to figure out entrance to be ignored by the staff who acted inconvenienced that we were trying to pay admission, we knew that we were not going to enjoy this museum. While some of the artwork was interesting and thought provoking, most tried too hard to be different and came across as either extremely sadistic or as boring as a library bookshelf. Next time I venture near Little Tokyo, the Geffen at MOCA won't be on my agenda.<//Text>

<review>I went to MOCA this past Saturday for the Hello Kitty Convention it was extremely small venue for all the attendees.

I been a fan of Hello Kitty since my sister introduced me to her at a very young age with pencils, stationary, and pencil boxes you name it! Now, we are able to enjoy it with her girls at the Hello Kitty Con. I got us all tickets to attend the Hello Kitty Con and it was a great experience to share this with them and my other girlfriends and their daughters as well.

Let's get to the juicy details of the HK Con.

- I heard about the insane lines after lines through two elite yelpers and realized with kids going with us it's not a good idea to go early so we got there at 11am.
- We parked at a $6 parking structure off of Commerical & Alameda Ave. It was a far walk to MOCA but it wasn't too bad.
- To our surprise, there's still a long line to get in but it wasn't too bad.
- As we waited in line, the workers/staff were handing out pins, stickers, HK rings, and smiles =) everywhere.
- Although, the lines were super long, everyone was tolerable of the wait and was showing a lot of excitement.
- There were vendors/licensees that sold HK products in the Supermarket area.  I got a souvenir HK sweater and custom made shirt. Everything was pricey of course so you had to pick and choose what you wanted.
- I didn't bother with the shop upstairs since it was 3-4 hour wait and it reminded me of the shop at Puroland in Japan so why bother.
- Their were a lot of photo op everywhere and it was so fun to take so many pictures of the arts, decor, vintage HK stuff, and awesome back drops in every room!
- We were extremely disappointed in TARGET collaboration with HK in the Carnival Room. We waited about 2 hours to get in line and we were almost at front when they announced they were no longer letting people inside. The security guards didn't even communicated that the line was cut short and that they were no longer accepting people inside. The people inside took their time playing the games. I feel bad for our kids and other kids waiting to play games.
- Outside, they had a fake tattoo area, nail shop, caricature area, pumpkin patch, penny machine, arts & crafts, and a huge line for the shop.
- There ware food trucks outside with long lines. I think they should've had more food options. So, luckily we ate before going and were okay all day.
- My favorite was seeing Hello Kitty two times and Yuko Yamaguchi.  I missed out on all the freebies like free drawn picture, signing, and classes that were sold out.
- We stayed until 7pm even though they were closing until 9pm for HK Birthday. We missed our free opportunity to go to the Japanese Museum.

Overall, it was a enjoyable experience but I would complain about the venue being small, long lines, and the collaboration with Target being unorganized.

I'm glad my friends and I had a great time regardless. I know Sunday is madness. Good luck to the attendees on Sunday.< /review>< pics>
None< /pics>
